The heads of the Provincial Government's Construction Department, the Municipal Government's National Products Exhibition Hall, and representatives from the Shanghai National Products Merchants Association all gave speeches, expressing their hope that the government and the people would unanimously support the development of national product factories and make every effort to stop foreign goods. The exhibition is scheduled to last for three weeks, with 80 national product factories participating, creating a very enthusiastic atmosphere. (Central News Agency dispatch from the 20th)

Zhejiang Security Department Burns Narcotics 101

(Hangzhou) The Zhejiang Security Department publicly burned narcotics on the morning of the 20th. These were confiscated after being discovered being transported by unscrupulous military officers. (Central News Agency dispatch from the 20th)

Appropriation of Funds for Disaster Relief in Chongming after Windstorm 102

(Zhenjiang) The Jiangsu Provincial Government reported that a hurricane had caused a disaster in Lishan, Chongming, but due to the Provincial Treasury's financial constraints, it was unable to provide relief. Therefore, it telegraphed the Ministry of Industry and Commerce, instructing the Jiangsu-Zhejiang Fisheries Improvement Association to allocate funds for relief from the collected fisheries construction fees to assist the disaster victims. (Central News Agency dispatch from the 20th)

Japanese Troops in Northern Manchuria Reconnoiter Soviet Russian Military Preparations 103

Dispatch of Puppet Ships to Navigate the Heilongjiang and Ussuri Rivers

Soviet Russian Naval and Air Forces Meet with Head-on Demonstrations

The Anti-Japanese National Salvation Army Active in the Four Counties of Eastern Jilin

Harbin Communication: Since the Japanese army invaded Northeast China, the international rivers between China and Russia have not seen Chinese merchant ships for more than a year. This year, after the Heilongjiang and Ussuri Rivers thawed, the puppet navigation bureau used the excuse of opening the navigation routes on both rivers to actually reconnoiter the movements of the Soviet Russian Far East Army. It first dispatched the "Harbin" and "Shanghai" ships to the Heilongjiang River, reaching as far as Heihe, and they were able to reach their destination safely. During the journey, they passed the Russian shore without encountering any obstacles. Therefore, the bureau believed that the navigation of the Ussuri River should be no problem. On May 22nd, it again dispatched the "Ping'an" and "Tongshan" ships to sail down the river. The "Ping'an" arrived at Hulin, the last pier on the Ussuri River, before the "Tongshan." Although it was pursued by Russian ships during the voyage, there were no accidents. Only when passing through Suiyuan County, where Yuan Futing's National Salvation Army was stationed (some say that Yuan is Yuan Chonggu, the commander of the reclamation army during the Jiangqiao battle in the winter of the 20th year of the Republic), the National Salvation Army sent soldiers aboard to inspect the ships and escort them. On the return trip, they were not allowed to carry merchants and residents from Hulin, Raohe, and Suiyuan counties for export, but there were no other disturbances. When "Ping'an" returned to Tongjiang, "Tongshan" saw that it had returned safely and, carrying out the orders of the puppet navigation bureau, continued its navigation. When passing the base of the Russian River Defense Fleet at Xu'ergu on the Russian shore, six of its warships sailed out, surrounded "Tongshan," and anchored in the middle of the river. The Russian Marines boarded the ship and searched for Japanese officers and Russians. They arrested twelve White Russian employees, and then released the ship, which continued to sail downstream. Upon reaching Hulin, it was detained by the National Salvation Army and ordered to travel back and forth between the three counties of Hu, Rao, and Suiyuan for military and commercial transportation. After the ship was detained, the puppet state was greatly angered and sent Shi Liben, a special envoy from its diplomatic department stationed in Harbin, to protest to Russia, saying that the National Salvation Army was an anti-Manchu army nurtured by the Soviet Union and that it should immediately release the "Tongshan" merchant ship. The Russian side instructed its consul in Harbin to reply that the detention of "Tongshan" had nothing to do with Russia and that only the White Russian employees on the ship had been arrested for interrogation due to their military espionage activities. Seeing that the protest was ineffective, the puppet state vigorously built new river defense warships, a total of five, which were secretly built at the Osaka Shipyard in Japan last year and shipped to Harbin this year to be assembled. They were completed one after another in mid-June, namely "Datong," "Limin," "Enmin," "Pumin," and "Huimin." The ships were extremely small, with a draft of no more than one foot and five inches, carrying 25 crew members, and could travel 60 li per hour with the current. They were fast river boats powered by light gasoline, and each boat could be equipped with several light and heavy machine guns. The Japanese, who were manipulating behind the puppet state, believed that with such new river defense equipment, they had more than enough to deal with Russia. Therefore, in mid-July, after the five ships were launched one after another, Yin Zuogan, the commander of the puppet river defense fleet, led "Enmin," "Huimin," "Pumin," and the old river defense ships "Lisui," "Jiangqing," and "Jiang'an," a total of six ships, and supervised and commanded by a group of Japanese sailors, and sailed downstream overnight. The original plan was to sail directly to the Ussuri River, partly to demonstrate against Russia and to create a strong intimidation for the Tokyo Conference on the sale of the East Railway, and partly to attack the National Salvation Army and recapture the "Tongshan." By the 29th, the ships had passed Tongjiang, and by the 31st, they had sailed out of Sanjiangkou. Before reaching Xu'ergu, more than ten Russian warships sailed down the river to intercept them, and seaplanes were also flying in the air. The extent of their demonstration against the puppet state was even greater than that of the puppet state. Seeing the strength of the Russian navy and that its warships were all large and sturdy, with firepower far superior to that of the five newly built ships of the puppet state, the puppet state was concerned that there might be danger in returning after sailing to the Ussuri River, and especially feared that the Russian ships would cut off their retreat. Therefore, they sailed to Molihong outside Sanjiangkou and anchored, sending people to negotiate with Russia to explain the true intention of sailing to the Ussuri River. The Russian side replied that although the Heilongjiang and Ussuri Rivers were international rivers in the past, China has never had the right to sail warships on them. Since the Heilongjiang and Ussuri Rivers are close to the Russian border, they are like inland rivers of Soviet Russia. Therefore, the security of all the river surfaces is maintained by Soviet Russian warships, and there is no need for Chinese warships to come, lest misunderstandings occur. If the Manchurian state really wants to attack the National Salvation Army, it may as well send troops by land, why send warships and make Soviet Russia suspicious. After receiving the reply, the puppet fleet commander Yin Zuogan did not dare to lead the fleet directly forward, so he telegraphed the puppet government for instructions, and at the same time sent a letter to Yuan Futing, the commander of the National Salvation Army, requesting the release of the "Tongshan" ship, otherwise the army, navy, and air force would attack together. Yuan replied that if he wanted the "Tongshan" to return, he must send another merchant ship. Seeing no results, Yin led the fleet back to Tongjiang on August 2nd. On the 7th and 8th, the ships sailed back to Harbin in two batches. This demonstration by the six ships against Russia ended in failure. However, the Japanese were very eager to find out about the Soviet Russian naval armaments, intending to prepare for an attack in case the Sino-Russian War broke out on the day of the rupture of the Eastern Railway negotiations. Therefore, Kobayashi, the Rear Admiral of the Japanese naval commander stationed in Manchuria, departed on August 3rd aboard the "Guangning" river warship, intending to first reconnoiter along the Heilongjiang River and then go to the Ussuri River, ostensibly to explore the location of gold mines. On August 7th, the ship arrived in Tongjiang. Rumors that the Russian side had already prepared a protest, saying that the Ussuri River and the Heilong River were international rivers between China and the Soviet Union, and that warships flying the Japanese flag could not enter, dampened Kobayashi's trip to Heihe. In the Hulin area, the strength of the National Salvation Army was very strong. Those belonging to Yuan Futing numbered about 20,000, and those belonging to Chen Dongshan numbered about 30,000. Liu Wankui's branch was recently organizing training near Baipaozi in the Xingkai Lake area and contacting the local patriotic volunteer army, also numbering around 20,000. Mishan County was recovered by Chen Dongshan's army on August 6th. Therefore, the four counties of Jidong, Hu, Rao, Sui, and Mi, are still within the sphere of influence of the National Salvation Army. However, in mid-August, the puppet state river defense fleet sailed to the Ussuri River for the second time. It was heard that on the 21st, it passed Suiyuan and went upstream, directly to Hulin. The Hulin National Salvation Army was attacked by the Matsuda Regiment and Hamada Detachment of the Japanese 10th Division and the puppet state army from Mishan, and were attacked from both front and back, and had to retreat temporarily to the Gushanzishan area. A part of Chen Dongshan's army temporarily retreated to Baoqing. The puppet state river defense warships were able to reach their destination along the river without obstruction, retrieve the two merchant ships "Tongshan" and "Beizhen," and sailed back to Harbin on September 9th. Although the righteous army retreated temporarily, it was only for strategic reasons. After the puppet state river defense fleet left, they returned to Hulin and Suiyuan. (September 10th)

Review of the Xinjiang Rebellion 104

The Story of Yang Zengxin's Assassination and the Reasons for Jin Shuren's Expulsion

Huang Musong's Mission of Appeasement was Ineffective, Luo Wengan Continued to Soothe and Pacify

The "North China Daily News" of Peiping (Beijing) reports that a Westerner recently returned from Xinjiang, discussing the origins of the new changes, which in reality contain ethnic meanings. Adding to this is the presence of foreigners, with mutual animosity between White Russians and Red Russians, leading to further exacerbation. The entangled Hui people have come to be divided into two, mutually incompatible. Tracing the origins of the entangled Hui, they are in fact of Turkic origin, with pointed heads and noses, and mostly bearded. One part resides in the plains, in cities and towns, specializing in farming, while others live in the valleys, mostly engaged in animal husbandry. Another type is a mixed race of Arab and Han people, called the Donggan, that is, the commonly known "Hui Hui." Although these two groups belong to the same Islamic faith, they are extremely incompatible, like ice and charcoal. Therefore, the Chinese government often utilizes this opportunity to control this remote province. Aside from these two groups, there are also some Han Chinese, including bureaucrats, soldiers, merchants, and workers from Shandong Province. Although their numbers are not large, their potential power is considerable, and they often follow the lead of the central government, as their situation dictates. The Russians who have recently entered Xinjiang, although few in number (approximately 10,000), are very influential in Xinjiang's politics. Red Party members are mostly attached to the Russian consulates and the Soviet Russian import and export companies. The White Russians are those who fled to Xinjiang Province from Russian Turkestan in the eighth year of the Republic, due to their inability to tolerate the oppression of the Red Russians. At that time, the Xinjiang government wanted to recruit them to quell the Hui rebellion, and specifically threatened that if they did not serve China, they would be sent back to Russia. In order to save their lives, these people had no choice but to be employed by the new government. In this way, 4,000 White Russians were recruited and equipped with weapons to quell the rebellion, like crushing dry weeds. The Xinjiang government has been able to maintain security in recent years, largely relying on their strength. Unexpectedly, those of different races have different hearts. In the future, the rebellion will not come from the rebellious entangled Hui, but from the White Russian soldiers relied upon as the Great Wall.

Yang's Assassination 105

Yang Zengxin's governance of Xinjiang was quite fair and selfless, so Xinjiang was peaceful at that time, and travelers did not fear thieves. In the whole country, Xinjiang was truly second to none. Unexpectedly, four years ago, Yang was assassinated, and the situation changed greatly. At that time, a certain Fan coveted political power and, taking advantage of Yang's public banquet at the Diplomatic Office, suddenly assassinated him. His arrangements can also be said to be very meticulous. It is not known whether red elements were involved in the conspiracy, but it can be asserted that they were inciting the chaos. Unexpectedly, Fan's reputation was not well-received, and the soldiers did not obey, eventually leading to chaos. Fan also paid the price for his crimes. Therefore, Jin Shuren, a key member of the Kuomintang, took the stage and became chairman. The winds and clouds met, and the National Government also trusted him. Only then did he hold great power and suddenly become the leader of the people. After Jin took office, he was opposed by all parties, and he himself was very mediocre, with no achievements. His first policy was to amass wealth, increasing taxes and levies, so that the people could not live. In addition, he greatly reduced personnel, replacing them with people he brought in. All of Jin's relatives, old friends, and those who usually fawned on him were promoted overnight. Since these people came to make a fortune, how could they let go of any opportunity? Knowing that they would only be officials for a short time, would they not desperately exploit the people? Due to ethnic concepts in that area, intermarriage between Hui and Han has not yet become widespread. Han women rarely marry into the remote border areas. The people used by Jin often forcibly seized women from the people, leading to deeper and deeper hatred. Jin himself lived in seclusion and remained in the government office all day long. Even if he occasionally went out, he would always be hidden in an armored car, never daring to show his face. To this day, the people of Xinjiang do not know whether Jin is fat or thin, unlike Yang, who traveled lightly and often socialized with the local elders.

The Entangled Hui Rebellion 106

In the 19th year of the Republic, after Yang's position became vacant, the Hui people saw that political affairs were neglected, and so in the eastern part of Xinjiang, they openly raised arms and revolted. The Hui bandit leader Ma Zhonglin again led bandits from Gansu to assist them. Because the government soldiers' weapons were sharp, they were easily defeated. If they had been handled seriously, it would not have been difficult to resolve the issue fundamentally. However, the Chinese government never handled things thoroughly. Allowing the bandits to exist was a way to raise soldiers. If the bandits were wiped out, then the soldiers would have no use. As a result, the entire province spread, and all places were lost. By the 22nd year of the Republic, Ma Zhonglin rebelled again and attacked various parts of Xinjiang. Hui bandits rose up in response. Hami was lost, and Ma immediately attacked Dihua. Jin then sent White Russian troops to defend it, and they won a great victory. If they had taken advantage of the victory to pursue and suppress the rebellion, it would not have been difficult to wipe it out in one fell swoop. However, Jin felt that he had no kindness to the Hui people and was deeply afraid that the people's hearts would change, endangering his own life. He quickly ordered the troops to return to defend Dihua. At that time, three thousand men under Generals Ma Zhanshan and Su Bingwen happened to be returning to the country from Russia, passing through Dihua. If Jin Shuren could have treated them with sincerity and recruited them for his own use, the Hui rebellion in Xinjiang would not have been so serious, and order in various places could have been restored immediately. Ma and Su's old troops were all veterans who had survived hundreds of battles and had fought bitterly with the Japanese army in Heilongjiang, experiencing dozens of battles. Jin was suspicious by nature and only gave them a few weapons as a perfunctory measure. From then on, the northeastern heroes also felt disheartened. Later, they mostly took a wait-and-see attitude towards the rebellion, and eventually took concerted action with the rebel party. If Jin had not provoked them, who would have believed it? By this year, if Jin had not deducted the White Russian troops' pay and rations, things would not have reached an uncontrollable point. Jin was quite xenophobic, as evidenced by his high-handed treatment of the Sino-French academic expedition. Afterwards, he became close to the Red Army, and the White Russian troops' pay and rations were not paid. This spring, Kashgar and other places in the northeast rebelled one after another, with great momentum. Jin ordered the White Russian troops to go out and conquer, but unexpectedly, the soldiers, who had not been paid for months, resisted and refused to obey. The northeastern heroes who had returned to the country from Russia also stayed in Dihua and delayed. The rebels were gradually approaching the provincial capital. Before long, the White Russian troops sent Jin an ultimatum, urging him to step down immediately, guaranteeing his safety, and promising to escort him to Russia, declaring their support for Liu Wenlong, the director of the Education Department, as the provincial governor. Because Liu was popular and the position of provincial governor was only nominal and a figure of transition. At this point, Jin was still reluctant to give up his post. After the deadline passed, there was no response. At this point, the White Russian troops joined forces with Ma and Su's old troops to jointly take action against Jin, surrounding the government office and fighting fiercely with his guards for two days. Jin's personal property was burned and looted, and as many as 4,000 guards were killed. Jin disguised himself and fled at night, reaching Chugurchak on the Russian border, and from there returned to Tianjin. From then on, he could live a leisurely life and enjoy his remaining years. Although Dihua had undergone a rebellion, the people suffered very little, which was a comforting thought. As the war was coming to an end, the central government sent Envoy Huang Weixian to Dihua to comfort and pacify the people, and planned to disband the Xinjiang government. Unexpectedly, Huang's relationship with all parties soured as soon as he got off the train. Before declaring the central government's wishes, he first became a prisoner. Afterwards, after repeated mediation, he was allowed to return south by plane. As far as this reporter knows, Huang said that everything had been settled and boasted shamelessly. We cannot help but thank Huang for his ability to mediate. After Huang returned, Foreign Minister Luo personally came forward. The central government immediately recognized Liu Wenlong as chairman, and the leaders of Kashgar and other places came to submit. The central government's authority was still in effect, but examining the actual situation, it is doubtful whether it can last. Foreign Minister Luo, as a senior official of the central government, took on the heavy responsibility of mediating disputes and pacifying the Hui people, so that the northwestern key town would listen to the government's command. His hardship and dedication are self-evident. Let us wait and see.

The Recovery of Kaihua County 107

The Red Bandits of Fang and Shao Captured the County Seat on the 17th, Which Has Been Recovered by the Security Team and Xing's Division. The Bandits Are Fleeing to Wuyuan and Other Places in the Northwest.

Hangzhou Communication: Kaihua County, Zhejiang Province, was captured by the Red Bandits of Fang and Shao taking advantage of the opportunity on the 17th. It was recovered on the 18th by the Third Regiment of the Security Team and Xing Zhennan's Division. The bandits are fleeing to Wuyuan and other places in the northwest. They are being pursued. The text of the telegrams received by the Provincial Government from various parties yesterday (20th) is recorded as follows: (1) Kaihua County Magistrate Qiao telegraphs, (At dawn on the 17th of this month, more than 5,000 Red Bandits, with approximately 1,000 rifles, as well as machine guns, hand-held wooden shell hand grenades, etc., surrounded and attacked the west, south, and north gates of the subordinate county. My county's basic team, the fifth and sixth detachments, the second district team, in addition to sending scouts to guard the blockhouses, only had 52 team members to resist the bandits for about one hour, killing more than ten bandits and wounding more than twenty. Four of my team members died and five were injured. The incident was sudden, and the troops stationed in Huabu did not have time to rescue them. My team was outnumbered and the bandits swarmed into the city, emptying the prison. As a last resort, we retreated outside the east gate across the river. The bandits crossed the river and pursued us in large numbers. We continued to retreat to Sanliting, waiting for reinforcements before launching a counterattack. By 8:00 PM that day, my team had not received reinforcements and dispersed into various mountain valleys, firing shots one after another. The bandits suspected that reinforcements had arrived and retreated westward at about 10:00 PM that night. At 5:00 AM this morning, I led the team into the city to maintain order. This time, the county seat suffered a terrible bandit robbery. The government agencies and the masses suffered heavy losses, and many men and women were captured.) (2) Hao, the Third Sub-district Director of Security stationed in Quzhou, telegraphs, (1. According to reports from various counties, the bandits who captured Kaihua this time are called the Fourth Division, numbering three to four thousand, with about one thousand guns, eight machine guns, and a commander named Zhou. They also have Mao Zedong's proclamations. They entered the city on the morning of the 17th. On the morning of the 18th, knowing that our reinforcements had arrived in Huabu, they retreated at noon, claiming to attack Wuyuan, etc. 2. I have sent Inspectors Jiang Zhihang and Commissioner Wang to Kai to assist County Magistrate Zhu in handling the aftermath.) (3) Wang Hantao, the Administrative Inspector Commissioner of the First Special Zone, telegraphs, (I arrived in Huabu at 4:00 PM. I learned that 1. Jiang's regiment entered Kaihua City on the morning of the 19th. The Red Bandits fled from the eleventh district of the west township. County Magistrate Zhu also returned to the city to take office on that day. 2. The Red Bandits who entered the city numbered approximately 3,000. 3. To prevent bandits from infiltrating, I have personally discussed with Deputy Division Commander Song to send troops to search and suppress them immediately, in order to eliminate them. 4. I will go to Kaihua on the morning of the 20th to discuss the aftermath with County Magistrate Zhu.) (4) Zhang Xianyi, County Magistrate of Changshan, telegraphs, (According to reliable reports, the bandits of Kaihua retreated in two groups. The majority retreated towards Majinling via Zhangcun and Zhongcun, and a part retreated towards Baishaguan. When passing through Baishaguan on the morning of the 18th, they came into contact with Shi's regiment. After holding each other for about one hour, they fled westward. At the oil creek pass. There are still sporadic scattered bandits on the nearby mountains. Deputy Division Commander Song is sending troops to suppress them. The 1st Battalion and 3rd Company of my Jiang regiment, except for the 13th company, which is still stationed in Kaihua, returned to Huabu on the night of the 19th.) (September 20th)

Chiang Orders the Abolition of Redundant Agencies in Jiangxi, Hubei, Hunan, and Anhui 108

Transferring Funds to Supplement County Administration Expenses

And Promulgating County Administration Guidelines

Nanchang Communication) Chairman Chiang has emphasized that this campaign to suppress bandits should be based on the principle of "30% military, 70% political," and that in the political aspect, the county is the starting point and the destination. Therefore, the selection of county magistrates is extremely important. He has repeatedly ordered the provincial governments to select intelligent and capable individuals who can reverse the chaos to fill the positions. At the same time, he has also ordered the county magistrates in the bandit areas to abandon their mentality of seeking personal comfort and avoiding responsibility, and to be determined to share the weal and woe of the people and to coexist with the city. However, since the responsibilities of county magistrates are so heavy, their treatment should be improved. In addition to appointing the county magistrates in the bandit suppression areas as military judges to control everything, he has also ordered the troops stationed in various places to respect the county magistrates and enhance their prestige. He has also decided to expand the county administration expenses to achieve political effectiveness. He has also ordered various provinces to save wasteful expenses and transfer funds to supplement the county administration expenses. According to the Guling telegram, Chiang telegraphed Jiangxi, Anhui, Hubei, and Hunan on the 15th, ordering them to abolish all redundant agencies and all redundant personnel, and to use the funds saved to increase the county administration expenses. He also formulated four guidelines for refreshing county administration, ordering them to be carefully handled in consideration of the local environment. His telegram reads, (The county government is close to the people and is the foundation for promoting politics. The quality of politics depends on the integrity of the county magistrate. However, because the administrative expenses of various counties are too small, the county magistrate cannot afford to be honest and govern well. All kinds of corrupt practices are mostly caused by this. In order to rectify the situation, the county administrative expenses should be increased.) After receiving the telegram, Chairman Xiong of the Jiangxi Provincial Government immediately summoned the heads of various departments to discuss ways to reduce personnel and government expenditures and increase county administrative expenses, and presented the environmental needs of various counties in the province for approval, determining the steps to be implemented. (September 17th)

Shandong Relief Committee Distributes Central Government Relief Funds 109

Distributing According to the Severity of the Disaster, Kou Yingjie Donates 5,000 Yuan for Disaster Relief, Relief Committee Plans to Borrow 500,000 for Relief

Jinan Communication: The Central Government recently decided to allocate 500,000 yuan to provide relief for the Shandong disaster and telegraphed Han Fuju to first borrow the funds from the Shandong Provincial Government to provide emergency relief. The Provincial Government has successively advanced more than 200,000 yuan. Yesterday (17th), the Central Government remitted the first batch of relief funds of 100,000 yuan to Jinan. The Provincial Relief Committee immediately held a meeting to discuss the distribution method, but there was no result. At 10:00 AM this morning (18th), the Provincial Relief Committee continued to hold a meeting to discuss. Committee members Li Shuchun, Zhang Weicun, Zhao Xinru, Xin Zhujiu, He Supu, etc., agreed to distribute emergency relief according to the severity of the disaster in the severely affected areas, the second most severely affected areas, and the third most severely affected areas. Together with the 82,000 yuan of donations received from various parties before, a total of 182,000 yuan will be distributed. The personnel distributing the funds will still be Zhang Shouqian, advisor to the Provincial Government, for the south bank of the Yellow River, and Li Tianni, advisor, for the counties on the north bank. The Provincial Relief Committee will send personnel to assist. The number of relief funds to be distributed to each county is as follows: (1) Puyang, Fanxian, Shouzhang, Yanggu, Heze, Cao County, Juye, and Dong'a counties, each county previously received 6,000 yuan in donations, and now each county will receive an additional 7,000 yuan in Central Government relief funds. (2) Jiaxiang, Shanxian, Chengwu, Dingtao, Dongping, and Yuncheng counties, each county previously received 4,000 yuan in donations, and now each county will receive an additional 4,000 yuan in Central Government relief funds. (3) Jining, Yutai, Feicheng, Juancheng, Changqing, and other five counties, each county previously received 2,000 yuan in donations, and now each county will receive an additional 1,000 yuan in Central Government relief funds. In addition, 3,000 yuan will be allocated to Jining and 2,000 yuan to Wenshang. The Central Government relief funds will total 90,000 yuan. The remaining 10,000 yuan will subsidize the Heze disaster relief shelter with 6,000 yuan and the Shouzhang disaster relief shelter with 4,000 yuan. The Provincial Relief Committee also ordered various counties to quickly prepare for winter relief, considering that the autumn season is deep and the weather is getting cold, and winter is coming soon. They should handle the disaster relief shelters as appropriate, and the Relief Committee will provide appropriate subsidies for expenses.

Former Henan Military Rehabilitation Supervisor Kou Yingjie, because his hometown was severely affected by the disaster, specifically donated 5,000 yuan to provide relief to Dong'a and Shouzhang counties. Kou arrived in Jinan from Tianjin with the funds yesterday. Xu Zushan, the commissioner of Weihaiwei, is also concerned about the disaster victims and generously donated 1,000 yuan. The total of the above two donations is 6,000 yuan, which will be distributed by the Relief Committee.

The Provincial Relief Committee believes that the disaster area in Shandong Province reaches more than 20 counties, with millions of disaster victims. Relief for food and clothing requires a large sum of relief funds. Although the Central Government has promised to allocate 500,000 yuan, only 100,000 yuan has been remitted so far, and it is unknown when the rest will be remitted. Therefore, it is planned to request the Provincial Government to transfer 500,000 yuan from the Central Bank, which will be repaid by the relief funds allocated by the Central Government in the future. This petition is currently being drafted. (18th)

Songjiang: The Perilous Situation of the Songjiang Seawall 110

The Punan seawall in this county has been in a state of disrepair for years. Despite the provincial government allocating funds and manpower for large-scale repairs, the seawall's collapse has reached an extreme point. It has suffered repeated heavy damage from severe storms in July and August of this year. Furthermore, from the evening of the 17th to noon on the 19th, it was subjected to a continuous series of hurricanes, coupled with rain. Occurring during the autumn high tide season, the terrifying waves and surging tides pounded with immense force, threatening the mountains and creating a perilous situation all around. Li Yihua, the patrolling officer of the county, sent urgent telegrams to the county government, stating briefly: (At 12:00 last night, a southeast hurricane suddenly arose here, accompanied by torrential rain. Today, it is even more rampant, and the situation is more severe than before. The Songjiang seawall has long been in need of repair, and the dangers are numerous. Coupled with the autumn high tide season, it is difficult to guarantee that the raging waves and violent winds will not cause a major disaster. In addition to gathering the seawall chiefs to temporarily hire laborers for round-the-clock guarding to prepare for unforeseen circumstances, I respectfully telegram Your Excellency to quickly dispatch workers to assist, and also request that you forward this to the Prefect to allocate funds for repairs. Li Yihua, Songjiang Patrolling Officer, kowtows respectfully). Another telegram said: (I trust that Your Excellency has received my urgent telegram. Around 7:00 last night, the wind intensified, and after 10:00, the sea tide rose sharply. The terrifying waves and surging tides had the force of mountains collapsing. The tide water overflowed the seawall surface, making it almost impossible to stand. The magnitude of the wind and tide was rarely seen in recent times, causing widespread panic. I immediately led the seawall chiefs and laborers to transport sacks, floodgates, etc., to carefully protect the seawall. Fortunately, no major danger occurred. It was not until 3:40 this morning that the wind turned northwest, and the tide receded, that the situation stabilized somewhat. I immediately conducted a segment-by-segment survey and determined that from the first to the ninth sections, over 300 tree trunks had been broken. In the third section, more than half of the stone slope of the cement project was destroyed. Soil and stones in each section also had collapses and disturbances. Currently, the wind is still strong, and I am still leading laborers to intensify emergency protection. After the wind subsides, I will submit a separate detailed report. I respectfully telegraph this first. Li Yihua, Songjiang Patrolling Officer, kowtows).

Suzhou: Midwife's Surgery Leads to Two Tragic Deaths 111

Tang, the wife of Huang Heshang, a resident of No. 7 Xilong Lane in Fengqiao Town, is 30 years old and has already given birth to three sons. She recently became pregnant again. On the night before last (the 18th), she went into labor. Because the baby came out bottom first, the child's head could not emerge for a long time, and its limbs were moving erratically. The midwife, Cai Xu, actually used large scissors to cut off the fetus's head at the neck, causing the baby's head to become trapped in the mother's abdomen, resulting in two immediate deaths. The incident was discovered by the police, who arrested Huang and Cai Xu and brought them to the city. The local court dispatched a prosecutor to the village on the 20th to investigate. They found the body of the mother lying horizontally on a bed, covered in blood. The headless body of the child had already turned into a mass of blood and flesh, a truly tragic sight.

Pilgrims' Conflict Leads to Monk's Drowning 112

A monk named Genyuan from Shangkong Temple in Mudu Town, Suzhou, led over a hundred male and female pilgrims in four boats, towed by a small steamboat, to Longhua Temple for pilgrimage some time ago. However, while passing through the Dongtingzi Village area of Zhengyi, it was nighttime, and the engine of the steamboat suddenly broke down, so they stopped for repairs. The pilgrims fought over sleeping berths, resulting in a conflict, even shouting for help. The villagers mistakenly thought it was a bandit alert and reported it to the Zhengjie Security Corps, which immediately assembled urgently and set off in different directions to apprehend the "bandits." Upon reaching the destination, they learned the true situation and immediately returned in formation. At that time, the steamboat had also been repaired and continued sailing. Upon arriving in Kunshan, they discovered that the pilgrimage leader, Monk Genyuan, was missing. They suspected that he had fallen into the river during the commotion. His mother, Wang Ma, immediately disembarked and, along with many others, went to the docking location to search. They recovered the body yesterday at noon. The responsible police district reported this to the Kunshan County government, which dispatched personnel to investigate.

Wujiang: Local Butchers Petition in Beijing 113

The butchers of this county, feeling oppressed by the monopolistic merchants and burdened by the excessive tax increases, were unable to bear the pressure. Businesses in Zhenze and Pingwang once suspended operations, but no satisfactory solution was reached. Currently, all the butchers in the county held a meeting in Jiangji on the 18th, resolving to send four representatives – Yin Lianfang, Zhou Youqin, Jiang Liancheng, and Shi Tianqiu – to Beijing to petition for the removal of the monopolistic merchants. The representatives were scheduled to go to Beijing today (the 19th) to petition the Jiangsu Education Funding Management Office, determined to achieve the goal of replacing the monopolistic merchants.

Yangzhou: Tomb of Twelve Heroic Women Discovered North of Guanyin Mountain 114

Central Committee member Wang Boling, while residing in his hometown to care for his parents, would often venture into the suburbs in his leisure time to explore historical sites. Yesterday, the 18th, he, along with Wu Xiaoyuan, Wang Runquan, and others, visited the old site of Guangling City, the former capital of Emperor Yang of Sui, reaching about two li north of Guanyin Mountain (the northern wall of the former Sui city, known as Baogu City in the Tang Dynasty). Suddenly, they saw a desolate tomb mound, still standing tall. In the weeds, there was an overturned monument with eroded inscriptions. Upon further inspection of the reverse side of the monument, the writing appeared new, exceptionally elegant. They determined that it was the tomb of Madame Li, the wife of Luo Jingfu from Longyou County, Zhejiang. At the end of the Ming Dynasty, when Shi Kefa died valiantly and Yangzhou was subjected to looting and rape by Qing soldiers, Madame Li gathered all twelve women of her family in a building, set it on fire, and immolated themselves to preserve their chastity. Therefore, the prefectural school had a "Guangling Twelve Heroic Women Shrine," with Madame Li as their leader. After more than three hundred years, her hidden virtue and silent glory were discovered unintentionally. It is said that Central Committee member Wang praised their chastity and heroism and intends to repair the tomb to promote the hidden virtue of our women who resisted foreign invaders and preserved their honor.

Nantong: River Embankment Collapse Causes Severe Flood Disaster 115

In Nantong, on the 19th, violent winds and heavy rain struck, and the river tide rose furiously. From Xiangshan east of Langshan to Kuzi Port, large sections of the river embankment collapsed in over ten places simultaneously. The tide water rushed in, causing areas such as Gonggao, Huangma, Zilang, Dexing, Ziyang, and Langyin townships to be submerged under water, six or seven feet deep. Houses were destroyed, and countless people and animals were drowned. Various groups in the city have rushed to provide emergency relief and dispatched lifeboats to rescue men and women in the disaster area. The Embankment Protection Association has purchased large quantities of sacks, firewood, and stones to try to block the breaches. The scale of the disaster is significant. The Huangni and Huang'an mountains are currently submerged in water. The Embankment Protection Association has sent an urgent telegram to the provincial government requesting disaster relief.

Hangzhou: Sun Tonggang Flew to Anqing Yesterday Morning 116

After the young aviator Sun Tonggang flew from Shanghai to Hangzhou on the 11th, he was warmly welcomed by all sectors. Sun and his classmate Wang Zuwen spent days visiting scenic spots such as West Lake and Mogan Mountain. They originally planned to participate in the inauguration ceremony of the "National Salvation Aircraft" in this province, but the ceremony was postponed due to rain. Sun and Wang could not wait any longer and went to the Jianqiao Aviation School by car at 8:00 yesterday (the 20th) to bid farewell to Mao Bangchu and others. They then went to the airport to repair the aircraft. They took off at 9:20. Because the various government agencies were unaware of Sun's travel schedule, they were unable to arrive in time to see him off. Only Cao Baoqing, Deputy Director of the Aviation Administration, and many officers and students from the Aviation School were present. Before his departure, Sun told reporters that he was deeply grateful for the kindness of all sectors, but due to the urgency of time, he could not bid farewell to everyone individually. He would arrive in Anqing at 1:00 this afternoon. After a short rest, he would transfer to Hankou, stay for two days, and then fly to Changsha, before flying directly to Hong Kong and Guangzhou, completing his ambition to fly across the country.

Martial Law Command Executes Bandit 117

According to a report submitted by the Provincial Capital Public Security Bureau, the Zhejiang Provincial Capital Martial Law Command interrogated three bandits: Zhao Jinsheng, and suspects Lian Dumei and Xu A'na, along with items such as handguns, bullets, and bayonets. It was found that Zhao Jinsheng had conspired with Lin Jingyi and seven others who were at large on the night of April 7th of this year to rob the house of Cai Fengzhi at Xinqiaotou. After the robbery, they returned to the house of Kong Defa at No. 22 Sanguan Lane in this city. Subsequently, Kong and others sent four threatening letters to Cai Fengzhi, extorting a large sum of money. They agreed to hand over the money at Qianqiao around May 25th. The Public Security Bureau dispatched detectives and police officers in disguise. They found a loaded handgun on the spot and arrested Zhao Jinsheng, Lian Dumei, and the homeowner Xu A'na. Zhao Jinsheng confessed to the robbery. Except for Lian Dumei and the others who were transferred to the court for handling, Zhao Jinsheng was sentenced to death according to law. Yesterday (the 20th) at 8:00 AM, Zhao was taken to the scene of the incident, his identity was verified, and he was executed by firing squad.

Shanghai-Hangzhou Express Train Kills Worker 118

Lai Yucheng, a resident of No. 44 Muchang Lane in this city, was 55 years old and from Xiaoshan. He had been farming in his hometown. Recently, he came to Hangzhou and worked at the Tongfeng Rice Store in Song'er Lane. Yesterday (the 20th) morning, he was carrying rice and walking on the railway tracks near the train station when the 9:40 express train from Zhakou passed by. He was unable to avoid it and was crushed to death on the spot. The scene was bloody and tragic. The Railway Bureau reported this to the court for investigation and prepared a coffin for burial. Lai is survived by his wife and children, and the family is in dire straits. His family has requested the Railway Bureau to provide generous compensation.

Xiaoshan: Boat Overturned by Strong Winds, Many Drowned 119

The weather in Xiaoshan became bad on the night of the 17th, with strong winds and heavy rain that lasted for two days and nights. Countless houses and boats were blown down or sunk. On the night of the 18th, four houses collapsed in Tanglangyao, killing an elderly woman in her seventies and a five-year-old girl. Also, a rice boat in the Xiaoxi River was sunk by the wind. Since it was nighttime, the entire boat sank, causing a loss of over 5,000 yuan. Furthermore, a night boat at Yanglou Bridge was sunk by the wind, drowning five passengers and boatmen. By the morning of the 19th, their bodies had not yet been recovered.

Chairman Mayers of Sino-British Bank Arrives in Shanghai 121

Two Railway Administrations Held Banquet the Night Before Last

Central News Agency reports that Mr. S.F. Mayers, Chairman of the Board of Directors of the Sino-British Bank, arrived in Shanghai on September 10th aboard the Empress of Russia from England. His mission is to investigate the situation of the various railways in China invested in and built by the bank. Since the Shanghai-Nanjing and Shanghai-Hangzhou-Ningbo Railways were also built with loans from the bank, Huang Boqiao, Director of the Two Railway Administrations, and Wu Shaozeng, Deputy Director, hosted a banquet for Mr. Mayers on the evening of September 19th. Also invited were Mr. Davison and Mr. Pusey, representatives of the Sino-British Bank in China, Zhong Wenyao, Desborough, Biggers, Railway Department Advisor Cundill, former Two Railway Administrations Supervisor Huang Yichang, and financial leaders Zhang Gongquan, Qian Xinzhi, Xu Xinliu, Tang Baoshu, and Wen Tou. Director Huang first gave a welcome speech, followed by Mr. Mayers's reply. The banquet concluded on a joyful note. It is reported that Mr. Mayers will begin his investigation soon. Director Huang's welcome speech and Mr. Mayers's reply are recorded separately below.

Railway Administration Welcome Speech 122

During the banquet, Huang Boqiao, Director of the Two Railway Administrations, delivered a welcome speech, saying: "Today, I, together with Deputy Director Wu, represent the Shanghai-Nanjing and Shanghai-Hangzhou-Ningbo Railways in hosting a banquet for Mr. Mayers, Chairman of the Board of Directors of the Sino-British Bank, which is a very honorable and pleasant occasion. Everyone present probably already knows Mr. Mayers, so there is no need for a detailed introduction. Mr. Mayers came to China from England at the end of the 19th century. When he first came, he worked in the British Consulate. Later, in 1908, he was appointed as a representative of the Sino-British Bank and resigned from the consulate. He resided in China for a long time and only returned to England in 1926. Since 1927, he has served as the Chairman of the Board of Directors of the Sino-British Bank in London. Mr. Mayers is already aware that the January 28th Incident last year caused an unprecedented catastrophe for our two railways. We estimate that the total loss of assets was 3.6 million yuan, and the loss of business was 5.6 million yuan. Subsequently, the repairs and supplements, as well as the burden of renting houses due to the destruction of the Administration's offices, will total more than 10 million yuan. In addition, we have just experienced the world's great economic panic, and the passenger and freight transport of our two railways has also declined accordingly. In a few days, Mr. Mayers, if you go to our two railways to take a look, you will surely feel that this major blow still exists and cannot be restored in the short term, and it involves many places, and it cannot be restored alone. I and Deputy Director Wu were suddenly appointed by the Ministry of Railways at the end of last year and have been in office for nine months now. We are very ashamed that we have nothing to show for our achievements, but under the guidance of the Ministry of Railways and the support of the Sino-British Bank, there may be a few points that can arouse Mr. Mayers' interest. We owe a lot of principal and interest to the Sino-British Bank and are very uneasy about it, but in the past eight months of this year, we have paid more than 1.726 million yuan, and in the next few days, we can pay another 330,000 yuan. In addition, we have paid more than 476,000 yuan for the previous years' joint transportation debts of various railways, and more than 685,000 yuan for various materials debts, totaling more than 3.21 million yuan in accumulated debts. At the same time, we must know that in addition to repaying the accumulated debts, there are also various post-disaster reconstruction expenses after the January 28th Incident, which are paid from the normal income. The so-called post-disaster reconstruction includes repairing the damaged tracks, bridges, and houses. Many of the houses were completely destroyed. We think that from this, the economic credit of the two railways can be gradually established. This is one point. According to the General Affairs Office report, the salary expenses of the staff this year are expected to be reduced by 85,000 yuan, and the printing, stationery, medicines, and miscellaneous expenses are expected to be reduced by 200,000 yuan. According to the Materials Office report, the material costs were reduced by 100,000 yuan in the first half of the year, so the total reduction for the whole year can be 200,000 yuan. Although there are no statistics for other parts, it is probably possible to save money as well. Even according to what was said above, it is already close to 500,000 yuan. On the one hand, according to the Traffic Department report, the business in the past two months, although not as good as the same months in the previous year and peacetime, is already much better than the same months in the previous year after the restoration of peace. We think that from this, the economic capacity of the two railways can also be gradually restored. This is one point. In terms of all affairs, we are now investigating and researching at the same time. We want to change everything that is not perfect or satisfactory. Especially for business, we want to use automatic methods to solicit customers from all sides. The business office established on Jing'an Temple Road in Shanghai is an example. However, an old situation is not created in one day, and it cannot be reformed in one day. This is another point. We believe that when doing something, when it comes to economics, although there are many things to do, it always boils down to two sentences: increasing revenue and reducing expenditure. Increasing revenue can make more money, but the first step is to put down a sum of capital. For example, for the Shanghai-Nanjing Railway, to increase transportation capacity, double tracks should be added and Wusong Wharf should be established. For the Shanghai-Hangzhou-Ningbo Railway, to expand business, the Cao'e River to Qiantang River section must be completed, all of which require considerable funding. Reducing expenditure can save money, but sometimes you have to spend money first. For example, the Shanghai North Station now has only 14 telephones installed, which costs 1,200 yuan per month. If you set up your own switchboard, you can install 80 lines and only have 600 yuan of maintenance costs per month, which is certainly very economical, but the price of installing the switchboard is 10,000 yuan first. Also, like our current office buildings, we rent the Riverside Building, which costs nearly 6,000 yuan in rent every month, which is certainly not economical. If we can build our own, we can save a lot, but we must first raise a construction fee of several hundred thousand yuan. In this regard, we want to make more money and spend less money at the same time, but we have to spend more money first. This also requires Mr. Mayers' attention. We hope that the Sino-British Bank will provide more support in this area. Regarding the large number of staff employed by our two railways, which results in huge salary expenditures, we are often criticized by all parties. In fact, this situation has also accumulated gradually. The reason is that the number of people used in each department has never been stipulated. At present, we are doing a work, which is to review the current needs, estimate the future development, and determine the number of staff at all levels in each place, so that there can be a limit to the employment of staff in the future. There is another work, which is to adjust the talents, so that everyone can use their strengths, and if there are vacancies, they will not be filled unless absolutely necessary. Doing this gradually will definitely make the things we do and the people we use commensurate in the near future. In terms of me and Deputy Director Wu taking office, the salary expenditure of staff in various places has been reduced by about 85,000 yuan this year, which has been said above. We also want Mr. Mayers and the Sino-British Bank to pay attention to this. Mr. Mayers, this time you came to China to investigate the railways invested by the Sino-British Bank, and the first thing you saw was our Shanghai-Nanjing and Shanghai-Hangzhou-Ningbo Railways. We hope that Mr. Mayers can give us more valuable guidance. We are very happy to see Mr. Mayers come to China from afar, so that we can have an opportunity to exchange opinions on our two railways. We respectfully propose a toast to congratulate Mr. Mayers on the success of his trip and to congratulate Mr. Mayers on his health."

Mayers' Reply 123

Mr. Mayers then replied, saying in brief: "I am very grateful for the warm welcome from Director Huang and Deputy Director Wu. Now that I have had a sumptuous feast, I will not make a long speech. I will just say a few words briefly. Director Huang just said that I should come to guide, which is too polite. I firmly believe that the heads of Chinese railway administrations are mostly very capable and dedicated to their work, and they know very well what their current work is. Someone as mediocre as me, how can I have the qualifications to guide? But one thing I can say is to explain the opinions of London to the leaders in all aspects of China. I know that the Chinese railway administrators have encountered various difficulties in recent years, and most of these difficulties have occurred because they were completely unable to prevent them. However, if railway administration can be detached from political relations, most of these difficulties can be avoided. Therefore, we should be optimistic and believe that China's railways will soon be able to repay all their debts. What the British investors are happy about is the interest on their investments. According to their past experience, of the two countries in the Far East, the investment in one country is paid on time, while the other country often delays. An important part of British commerce is foreign investment. Now that commerce is depressed, most of their assets dare not be released. So I say that our Chinese friends should now establish credit, so that foreign investors will all believe that after the depression has passed, these investors will naturally come to invest continuously. Now there is not much time, and I cannot discuss Director Huang's speech point by point, but his achievements are remarkable, which is very worthy of praise. I will study his speech carefully in the next few days, and after I return to London, I will definitely tell all parties about it. Before I sit down, I respectfully raise my glass and wish Director Huang and Deputy Director Wu good health."

National Government Advisor Miller Arrived in Shanghai Yesterday 124

The Shanghai Evening Post and Mercury reports that Mr. Miller, advisor to the National Government, has returned to Shanghai today (20th) on the President Cleveland after a fourteen-month tour of Europe and the United States. It is said that after leaving China, he crossed the Atlantic eight times. Wherever there seemed to be a very important event happening, he would rush to it. He met with Finance Minister Song in Washington and other places. When the London Economic Conference was held, he stayed in London for six weeks and lingered in Geneva for some time. Three-fifths of his time after leaving China was spent in Europe. The first thing he should do after arriving in China is to examine recent events and observe the current situation. Although he is often in close contact with political circles, he has been away from China for a long time and still feels a sense of distance. According to reports, Mr. Miller is quite famous in European and American journalism. He founded Miller's Review of the Far East and The China Weekly Review and has written several books. There are quite a few foreigners serving as advisors to various departments of the National Government, but he is the only one who serves as an advisor to the entire government.

Emergency Repairs to Endangered Seawall 126

Jiangsu Provincial Government Replied by Telegram - Jiangsu Provincial Government Replied to the Telegrams from the Shanghai Chamber of Commerce and Local Coordination Association, saying: Received and reviewed the two telegrams from Shanghai Chamber of Commerce and Local Coordination Association. It has been verified that the Baotai seawall is in danger, and Zhang Junsheng, a technician from the Construction Department, has been dispatched to conduct an on-site survey. As for the emergency repair funds required, the government's committee has decided to approve the advance payment by Baotai and Jiaxing counties for official expenditure, and has instructed the county chiefs to comply. Tang Wenzhi's Telegram: A Fierce Hurricane Struck on the Evening of the 18th 127

Devastatingly, over seventy yards of the Liuhekou and Nanwangjia wharves, which were under urgent repair, and over sixty yards of the Yuebingtai and over ten yards of the main wharf project were completely washed away. More than four thousand sandbags were swept away, and dozens of wooden piles were broken. All efforts were in vain. The remaining height of the embankment surface varies from one, two, to three feet. At Wangjiazhai, a breach of more than five yards occurred, destroying several houses. At the north end of the Liuhekou North Taoist Temple, a breach of more than nine yards occurred, flooding several miles and submerging all fields and houses. More than ten yards of the earthen embankment were also destroyed, along with the concrete and stone workers. In addition, at the south end of the new project at Fangjia Yan, about fifteen yards of earthen embankment collapsed, and over one yard of the wide stone beach slope was completely destroyed. Furthermore, the stone beach slope below the cement foundation completely collapsed, and four sections of the embankment surface were washed away, each four to five yards long and over one yard wide. Moreover, at the north end of the new project, a total of over forty yards long and over two yards wide were destroyed at two locations, north and south. Over sixty yards of the stone beach below were washed away. In addition, north of the water arrow, over twenty yards of earthen embankment were washed away, with the remaining embankment surface only two or three feet high, on the verge of collapse, a very critical situation. In addition to the seawall technology patrol inspectors, Zhang and Zhu, telegraphing the Taicang County Magistrate Hong, the Seawall Protection Committee held an emergency meeting yesterday, and Tang Wenzhi telegraphed the Provincial Government, requesting the urgent allocation of large funds for emergency repairs and to plan for long-term solutions. The draft of the telegram is recorded as follows: To Gu, Chairman, and Shu, Director, of the Zhenjiang Provincial Government. On the evening of Qiao, a hurricane caused two hazardous situations on the Taicang dike. The situation is particularly serious. We implore you to quickly allocate large funds for emergency repairs and to plan for long-term solutions. (Signed) Tang Wenzhi, Taicang Seawall Protection Committee. Ge.

Shen Bureau Chief's Remarks: Both the east and west seawalls were reported to be in danger during the two hurricanes this month. Yesterday, according to remarks from Shen, Bureau Chief of the Municipal Works Bureau, the East Seawall of this city (located in Gaoqiao, Pudong), on the shores of the East China Sea, is over fifteen kilometers long. Most of it is an earthen seawall. Because the mud is easily eroded by tides and waves, protective engineering is selectively constructed. Although this construction can protect the seawall during normal high tides, it is still difficult to avoid overflow and breaches during abnormal typhoons and storm surges, such as the typhoon twenty years ago and this year's hurricane. Although repairs were made after the dangerous situation during the storm surge twenty years ago, due to limited funding, most of the projects were of a superficial nature, resulting in weak areas throughout the seawall. Therefore, it is to be expected that it cannot withstand the impact of typhoons and storm surges. On the 2nd of this month, the first hurricane struck, although not as severe as the one twenty years ago. However, the wind direction twenty years ago directly battered the seawall, and except for the top section being damaged, the rest was fortunately unharmed. This year's wind force, however, eroded along the seawall, and the entire seawall was attacked, so the degree of damage and danger is actually greater than twenty years ago. After the hazardous situation, the bureau reported to the municipal government for an allocation of 50,000 yuan, and workers were immediately dispatched to make every effort to plug the breaches. The remaining damaged earthen seawalls will be urgently repaired by separately hiring workers. If there were no secondary hurricane, some of it could have been repaired. As for the damage to the West Seawall (in Wusong), it is far less serious than that of the East Seawall. However, since the stone seawall there was destroyed in many places by Japanese naval gunfire during the January 28th Incident, it has not been thoroughly repaired, resulting in several places collapsing during the storm surge on the 2nd of this month. Among them, one place at Wu Mufeng had a breach of fourteen or five feet, which was more dangerous. The bureau dispatched seventy or eighty regular workers the night before this storm surge, using sandbags to plug it, but after the storm surge on the 18th, it was washed away again. Yesterday, the bureau again transported a large amount of sandbags for emergency repairs, and municipal committee members in the area hired many local laborers and mud workers to cooperate in the repair. At the same time, a special commissioner was dispatched to Songhu to supervise, in order to ensure thoroughness. In short, the first step for the current construction steps for the East and West Seawalls is to plug the breaches. The 50,000 yuan allocated by the municipal government will be used immediately, and it is expected that the emergency construction will be completed in the near future. The second step is the proper construction, which requires a substantial amount of money, and a plan is currently being drafted.

Gaoqiao Citizens' Telegram: Xie Bingheng and other citizens of Gaoqiao submitted a document to the Municipal Government: To Wu, the Mayor of Shanghai. The Gaoqiao Seawall has been in disrepair for years and is extremely dilapidated. Last autumn, there were dangerous situations during the flood season, and we repeatedly appealed to the government for emergency repairs, but they were not completely solidified. On September 2nd of this year, the first hurricane suddenly caused more than ten breaches, and the angry tide rushed in, causing widespread flooding. Even the strong stone seawall suffered collapses. We have flown reports to the government through the local associations, requesting urgent repairs, but after many days, no news has been received. Unexpectedly, yesterday a second hurricane came again, with surging sea waves and a dark sky. Its momentum was fierce, far exceeding the first time. The Gaoqiao seawall was fundamentally shaken by the first devastation. It has not been repaired, and has suffered another attack. In one night, dozens of breaches occurred. The torrent rushed down, and the houses were all in ruins. A bit of fertile land has turned into a vast sea. Residents were terrified in the middle of the night, not knowing where to escape. Above, torrential rain stripped their souls, and below, huge waves crashed against the sky. Cries of pain and anguish echoed, with nowhere to turn. The misery is so extreme that we cannot bear to describe it fully. We believe that if trickles are not stopped, they will become rivers. The dangerous seawall, which has been dilapidated for years, has suffered repeated disasters from wind and waves. Sitting idly by and not saving it will eventually lead to a major disaster. The people of the coastal area live within the territory and are subject to the government. A great government does not abandon even the smallest. Therefore, we urgently report the disaster, begging for our lives. We respectfully implore you to be mindful of these people and immediately carry out emergency repairs, so that those who are displaced can have a temporary place to live and not be exposed in the water country, living as neighbors to fish and turtles. This is our only hope. As we urgently send this telegram, we await your orders. Xie Bingheng, Ma Boshen, Huang Luzhan, Huang Shixi, Yang Yunming, Zhang Baikuai, Ling Zihe, Shen Yi Liu, Cai Ruchuan, Yin Shijie, etc. bow. Ge.

Qin Chengqing Dismissed: According to Xin Sheng She, the seawall embankment project in Wusong is still being repaired yesterday. Because the wind has subsided, the work is easier. Therefore, the repair projects along the seawall, such as at Tanjia Bang, Yang Wharf, and Shuchuan Wharf, have been mostly completed. However, the most important Wu Mufeng embankment was washed away by more than twenty feet during the heavy wind and rain the other day. After the Wusong District Municipal Committee hired workers to make every effort to repair it, Qin Chengqing, who was appointed by the Works Bureau on the 17th to supervise the emergency repairs in Songhu, only arrived on the 19th, causing the embankment to collapse and a dangerous situation to arise. After this matter was learned by Shen Yi, the Director of the Works Bureau, he dismissed the member due to the member's ineffective performance, delayed important public affairs, and immediately appointed a special commissioner to lead earthworkers to Songhu, together with the earthworkers hired by the municipal committee, to cooperate in the emergency repairs. As of yesterday afternoon, more than a dozen feet have been repaired. The remaining part of the project should be completed in the next few days. As for the seawall embankments along the northwest gates of Baoshan County, they were all repaired yesterday. According to personnel from the Wusong District Municipal Committee Office, the third day of the eighth lunar month is the time when the tide is most turbulent. The embankments along the seawall must be repaired before the deadline in order to escape the dangerous period. Otherwise, there is concern for future troubles, and there is still a risk of the embankments collapsing, and so forth.

After the Hurricane: Land and Water Transportation Resumes 128

Sea Routes Open: The sea routes of the Shanghai-Ningbo line, the Shanghai-Taiwan line, and the North and South Ocean lines all resumed normal operation yesterday. Those that had been sheltering from the wind outside the Wusong estuary have all sailed. The postal ship of the Great Britain Company also loaded cargo and left Shanghai. The Hexing Wheel of Zhaoxing came to Shanghai from Guangzhou. It encountered a strong wind on the way. Fortunately, the wind momentarily surged past the ship, so although it encountered danger, it was quickly safe. It can arrive tomorrow. The Sanbei Wanxiang Wheel, which was sheltering from the wind in Yangshan, and the China Merchants Yushun Yuanan, etc., also telegraphed that they were safe and sound. They can all arrive in Shanghai today. The Kanhua Wheel of Changxing encountered a hurricane in the Pacific Ocean on the 17th, damaging the hull and injuring six sailors. It returned to Yokohama, Japan, for repairs. Yesterday, a telegram was received reporting that the repairs have been completed and it has set sail. The schedule will not be delayed.

Songhu Train Operates: The Songhu train could not reach Baotai Wan for two days. Now that the tide at Zhanghuabang has receded and the railway bridge over Yunzaobang has been urgently repaired by the railway bureau, the work has also been completed. Since 9:30 yesterday morning, the Songhu train has been operating normally, directly reaching Baotai Wan.

Telephone Lines Repaired: The Shanghai Telephone Bureau of the Ministry of Communications suffered heavy losses to all South City and Zhabei lines due to the hurricane on the 2nd of this month. It took two days and nights of urgent repairs to restore them. On the 18th, it was struck by another hurricane. According to Bureau Chief Xu yesterday, the losses this time were even heavier than the previous time. It is estimated that about 400 households in the South City district and about 100 households in the Zhabei district were affected. Especially in the Pudong and Longhua areas, many wooden poles were knocked down. This is because all the trunk lines in the Pudong district are old and dilapidated ones formerly owned by the Shanghai Telephone Company. Therefore, they were often broken by hurricanes. New poles have now been erected, and preparations are being made to establish a branch bureau. Moreover, the bureau's jurisdiction is vast, and places such as Wusong and Pudong are quite far from the bureau, so all the workers feel that they are not sufficient to be dispatched in emergencies. Due to the above-mentioned difficulties, there was a slight delay. Yesterday morning, a worker from the bureau, Huang Jintao, touched a power line while urgently repairing the lines at Xiaoximen, resulting in an accident that caused his death. The long-distance international radio station lines were also damaged. Workers are now being dispatched day and night to urgently repair them, and they have been gradually restored. It is expected that they will be completely repaired tomorrow.

Fishermen and Merchants Suffer Losses: According to the Central News Agency, according to news from the fishing and merchant circles in this city, the Xiangshan Port waters of Zhejiang suffered severe damage from the typhoon. Fishing boats there did not know that the hurricane was coming in advance, so they did not have time to take precautions. About forty boats capsized, with very heavy losses. The number of deaths is probably not small, but there is currently no confirmed information. As for the disaster situation in the fishing areas of Zhapu and Shenjiamen Bay, no reports have been received yet.

The Northeast Volunteer Army Relief Association Appeals for Aid on Behalf of Zhang Jidong 130

A letter requesting assistance from the Jilin Headquarters

The Northeast Volunteer Army Relief Association received a letter yesterday from Zhang Jidong, a representative of Song Guorong, the commander of the Provisional Second Army of the Jilin Volunteer Army, who came from Beiping, appealing for assistance. The association immediately replied with a letter, and at the same time sent a letter to the General Headquarters of the Jilin Volunteer Army requesting a modification of assistance and other matters. Excerpts from the three letters are separately recorded below.

Letter from Zhang Jidong 131

Respectfully, our army, since August last year, was ordered by President Zhu of the Yuanji Relief Association to appoint Song Guorong as the commander of the Eighth Route of the Northeast Volunteer Army (defense area: Panshi, Yitong, Shuangyang, Huadian, Changchun, Jilin), and held a swearing-in ceremony on August 9 in Heishi Town, Panshi County. Within a few days, it captured Panshi, Yitong, Shuangyang, Huadian, and other counties in succession. More than 40,000 people came to join us, with complete firearms and horses, and the momentum was huge, shaking the puppet capital. The Japanese and Manchukuo armies, seeing that the situation was not good, immediately mobilized a large force to suppress us. After more than ten days and more than twenty bloody battles, both sides suffered casualties. Later, due to a lack of ammunition, thin clothing for the soldiers, and no food, it was difficult to support them in the severe winter. Wounded soldiers also had no medicine or coffins. Therefore, the troops were reorganized into smaller units and worked separately. Our commander disguised himself and came to Beiping to seek assistance. General Zhu provided him with 15,000 yuan of current currency, promising continued assistance in the future. Commander Qi returned to the General Headquarters of Jilin in March of this year and served as the commander of the Second Army. He convened a meeting of anti-Japanese generals to reorganize. Seeing that the large gathering of troops in the past created a large target for the enemy and the work was small, this time, the troops were reorganized into smaller units, taking guerrilla tactics and implementing a joint defense system to help each other. The commander and cadres patrolled the defense area every week, issuing orders at any time and place, and gathering officers and soldiers to give speeches on the great righteousness of saving the country. Therefore, this year's work is incomparable to the past. This is the effect of having a small target. The detailed situation of the work has been reported to the General Headquarters of the Jilin Volunteer Army and forwarded to your association for the record. However, it is a pity that the work has lasted for seven months and has not received any assistance from any party. In a blink of an eye, the weather is cold, and the soldiers are thinly clothed and lacking food. This is the biggest problem. The former Jilin Headquarters pleaded for assistance for our army, and your association also sympathized with the hardships of the officers and soldiers and ordered the Jilin General Headquarters to appropriate funds from the remaining items of the 20,000 yuan agitation fee. After the representative learned of this, he immediately negotiated with the department. It said that there were only a few remaining, and the representative could do nothing. Now the soldiers are hoping for assistance, like clouds in a great drought. Therefore, I have described the general outline of the work and the difficulties currently felt. I want to disband the troops locally, but I am reluctant to abandon the good weapons to others, and there is no place for the patriotic athletes to return to. I want to continue the work, but I regret that there is no spiritual or material assistance, resulting in a dilemma. I sincerely ask you to sympathize with the tens of thousands of patriotic athletes and their officers and relatives, who are all in deep water, and do everything possible to provide assistance to solve the current difficulties.

Reply from the Relief Association 132

Respectfully, I have received your letter of September 14 and learned everything. Your army is loyal and courageous, resisting the Japanese Kou for the country, sacrificing and fighting, winning glory for the nation, and enduring hunger and cold, preserving strength for the country. I deeply admire all of these experiences. However, our association has already allocated the donations raised to various departments, and there are no remaining reserves. Recently, the relationship between investigating the national salvation donations has further interrupted the source of donations. I feel ashamed for the Guanwai athletes. A few days ago, Xiao Xiange, the standing committee member of the Jilin General Headquarters, came to Shanghai and met with him. According to him, the funds stored in the General Headquarters are quite different from what is stated in the letter. However, the department decided that the previously stored funds would be used exclusively for agitation fees and not for assistance. The above is the reason for the letter. I will now forward it to the department for appropriate accommodation, and I still ask you to contact the department directly to benefit the military. This is a special reply. I hope you will check and understand.

Letter to the Jilin Headquarters 133

Respectfully, according to the letter of September 14 from Zhang Jidong, the representative of Song Guorong, the commander of the Provisional Second Army of the Jilin Volunteer Army (the original text is omitted above). According to this, our association has already allocated the donations raised to various departments, and there are no remaining reserves. Recently, the relationship between investigating the national salvation donations has further interrupted the source of donations. A few days ago, Xiao Xiange, a member of your department, came to Shanghai on official business and met with him. He learned that the funds previously allocated were decided to be used exclusively for agitation fees and not for assistance. There are still many remaining funds at present. If the army is indeed making achievements in battle and is in a difficult situation, it seems that appropriate changes should be made and a little assistance should be provided to show encouragement. This has been decided by the Standing Committee of our association, requesting your department to investigate and handle it appropriately, and reply to Mr. Zhang, who will go directly to the front for contact on file. In addition to the reply, I hereby send a special letter for your reference.
